## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillations / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: The task involves acceleration dv_dt as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t, which describes the dynamics of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The physical relationships likely include restoring forces (functions of x), damping (functions of v), and possible external driving (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v
- Cubic stiffness (Duffing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v
- Pendulum equation: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) (nonlinear restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v - c1 * v * x**2 - c2 * x (self-excited oscillations)
- Driven damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t)
- Quadratic nonlinear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v**3
- Mixed nonlinear stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**2 - c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Parametric excitation: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v
- Cubic damping oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v**3
- Fifth-order stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5
- Forced with polynomial potential: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**2 - c2 * x**3 - c3 * v + c4 * sin(c5 * t)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative (energy-preserving) systems: dv_dt depends only on x, no v terms; dissipative systems include odd powers of v.
- Symmetric potential wells (e.g., quartic potential): restoring force contains only odd powers of x (x, x^3, x^5).
- Asymmetric potentials: even powers of x (x^2) appear in the force.
- Self-excited oscillations (e.g., van der Pol, Rayleigh): sign of linear damping term is reversed (negative damping for small amplitudes) producing limit cycles.
- Turbulent/high-speed damping: drag proportional to v*|v| or v^3 instead of linear v.
- External periodic driving: additive sinusoidal or cosinusoidal terms depending on t, with distinct frequency constant inside.
- Parametric forcing: stiffness coefficient multiplies a time-varying function (e.g., c(t)*x), leading to multiplicative time dependence.
- Small-angle approximation: sin(x) ≈ x for small x, making pendulum reduce to harmonic oscillator.
- Nonlinear stiffness softening/hardening: positive cubic coefficient gives hardening spring (frequency increases with amplitude); negative gives softening.
- Limit cycle existence: van der Pol type structure (v*(1 - x**2)) indicates self-regulation around a closed orbit.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO19)
============================================================
GT: -c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 53

**Step-by-step Analysis:**

The ground truth function is:
\[
f_{\text{GT}}(x, v, t) = -c_0^{\text{GT}} \beta \, v \;-\; \omega_0^{c_1^{\text{GT}}} \, x \, e^{-|x|}
\]
with fixed numerical values \(c_0^{\text{GT}} = 2\), \(c_1^{\text{GT}} = 2\), \(\beta = 0.2997749\ldots\), \(\omega_0 = -1.6718927\ldots\). This simplifies numerically to:
\[
f_{\text{GT}}(x, v, t) = -0.59954989233168\,v \;-\; 2.79522534599104\,x\,e^{-|x|}.
\]
The function depends only on \(x\) and \(v\); it is independent of \(t\).

Now examine Candidate 52:
\[
\text{Candidate 52: } c_0 v + c_1 x e^{c_2 |x|}.
\]
All constants \(c_0, c_1, c_2\) are free and can be assigned any real number (including zero).
